U.S. Naval Grand Maneuvers 21

More Than One Hundred Warships Participating

Three Hundred and Fifty Aircraft

San Pedro: The joint grand maneuvers of the U.S. Atlantic and Pacific Fleets opened on the 23rd to test the defense capabilities of the U.S. West Coast. One hundred and sixty-seven warships and three hundred and fifty aircraft participated, and an unprecedented grand maneuver was carried out under the scenario of a hypothetical enemy occupying the Hawaiian island of Oahu. The maneuvers will last seventy days. (United News dispatch on the 23rd) San Pedro: A portion of the U.S. Atlantic Reconnaissance Fleet has departed from the main naval base of the Atlantic Ocean to participate in the naval grand maneuvers. Admiral Leahy, Commander of the U.S. Joint Fleet, has decided to order the cruiser fleet to be stationed permanently in San Pedro, and explained the reason, saying that with the six-inch gun cruiser unit in the U.S. Atlantic Fleet permanently stationed in San Pedro, the result will be to increase the combat power of the Pacific Fleet. (United News dispatch on the 23rd)

Japan Dares Not Release Talk of Withdrawing from the League Again 22

Fearing Loss of Trusteeship's Right to Govern

Secret Military Deployments

Arising Concerns from All Sides

The League of Nations Administrative Council Will Submit for Discussion

Tokyo: According to diplomatic sources here, even if the League of Nations invokes Article 15, Paragraph 4 of its charter, Japan will not withdraw from the League of Nations, because once Japan withdraws, the right to govern the South Pacific Islands will inevitably be taken back by the League of Nations. According to the South Pacific Islands, if they are taken back by the League of Nations, Japan's power to wage war against the United States will be greatly reduced. Japan dares to openly provoke the United States in the Pacific, relying entirely on its submarine fleet based in the South Pacific Islands. Therefore, when the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs heard that the League of Nations had decided to invoke Article 15, Paragraph 4, it not only dared not express fierce opposition, but also telegraphed the Japanese representative not to declare withdrawal. It only ordered the Japanese representative to return home, but still expressed participation in the disarmament conference and the world economic conference convened by the League of Nations. Japan's move is to implement the strategy of obtaining its rights but not fulfilling its obligations, in order to wait for the self-destruction of the international community. (China United Press dispatch on the 24th)

London: The British Daily Express published a message on its front page today about Japan secretly building naval bases in the Pacific Islands. The newspaper's Geneva dispatch stated that reports on this matter will be submitted to the League of Nations Administrative Council this week. When the Japanese representative was questioned in a closed-door meeting of the Trusteeship Committee, he denied the news, but ultimately could not dispel the doubts about the events now discovered in the Mariana and Palau Islands. After repeated interrogations, the Japanese admitted that they had spent more than 100,000 pounds in British gold on naval bases and would continue to do so. According to reports, Palau Island was sold to Germany by Spain in 1899 and occupied by Australia in 1914. The Treaty of Versailles stipulated that this island be entrusted to Japan for administration. The Mariana Islands consist of fifteen islands of various sizes, originally owned by Spain. Among them, the largest island, Guam, was ceded to the United States in 1898, and the rest were sold to Germany the following year. In 1914, it was seized by Australia, and later Japan was also entrusted with trusteeship. (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

London: (Daily People's Voice) received a message from the newspaper's correspondent in Geneva, saying that there are rumors that Japan is establishing naval bases in the Pacific. The Administrative Council of the League of Nations will consider this news within this week. At a certain meeting, the Japanese representative was questioned in detail. The Japanese representative firmly denied this news, but people still worry about the situation in the Macao and other islands in the Pacific entrusted to Japan's rule. (Daily People's Voice) also stated that the earliest news about this matter came from the United States. Americans are extremely worried because if naval bases are built in the islands in the Pacific entrusted to Japan, it would not only violate Article 22 of the League of Nations Covenant, but also be greatly contrary to the Washington Four-Power Treaty. (According to Article 22, Paragraph 5 of the League of Nations Covenant, the entrusted state shall not build fortresses and naval and military bases within the territory of the trusteeship. The Washington Four-Power Treaty was signed by the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and Japan at the Washington Conference in 1921, and it is related to the Pacific Islands entrusted to Japan's rule.) (Havas dispatch on the 24th)

British Newspapers Comment on Recent Actions of the League of Nations 23

Both the London Labour Party's Daily Express and the Liberal Party's News Review discuss the importance of the League of Nations' drafting of a report on the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Daily Express stated, "The situation is serious, so the League of Nations must carry out its work with firmness and courage, but not with recklessness. The timidity and hesitation of last year resulted in nothing. This lesson still exists. If we merely approve the Lytton Report and attach a very vague narrative, and make hollow suggestions that China and Japan should seek an agreement based on the methods proposed by Lytton et al., then we are simply shirking responsibility. The League of Nations Assembly cannot use the Lytton Commission as a shield. The League of Nations will proceed, or should proceed, to what extent? This is an event that should be decided with an extremely calm mind. However, what we expect from the League of Nations is that the international community must have a practical and final determination not to wash its hands of this matter. Whatever the League of Nations can do, the League of Nations must not give up." The News Review stated, "Geneva has taken a sharp turn in the right direction. The League of Nations has only now launched its first initiative. To let the two parties handle the truth themselves is to allow them to start a war that endangers the world. Any war or war crisis is an event related to the League of Nations. This is a recognized doctrine. If the League of Nations abandons this doctrine, it would be very sad. Until yesterday, we did not dare to believe that the League of Nations would not abandon this doctrine. Now, it has determined its position, and the British government has clearly shown the world that Britain is a friend of the League of Nations. We do not want it to fight, nor do we want it to blockade Japan, but we want it to announce that no country is allowed to achieve its goals by methods that the world regards as intolerable." (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

London: The Times commented today on the final steps in the Manchurian problem, saying that those who criticize the League of Nations for hesitating and indecisive forget that changing with the times is sometimes the best policy among all policies. The Times quoted a letter from the daughter of former Prime Minister Asquith, published in the newspaper, saying that the League of Nations is not a supreme state, but a mechanism for passive or active joint policies. The Times also stated that there is indeed no necessary condition in the Sino-Japanese dispute case for the League of Nations to act, so the League of Nations can only draft what it considers possible and fair solutions, and the solutions must be sought along the outline of the Lytton Report. Unfortunately, Japan has rejected it with a completely unreasonable attitude, using this report as the basis for a solution. To make a moral judgment on any member is not the duty of the League of Nations membership. Japan is an important member of the League of Nations. If it understands the difficult position of the League of Nations and undertakes to abide by the recommendations of the League of Nations, then Japan can hope to restore its lost sympathy. The Times concluded that it is necessary to have strong domestic public opinion to make its government prepare to sacrifice lives and property to act against aggressor countries, and only then can this action be effective. (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

Resolutions of the Executive Yuan 24

Appoint Wang Dianzhang as Director of Civil Affairs of Shaanxi

Establish a French Consulate Branch in Lyon

Nanjing: The Executive Yuan held its 84th meeting on the 24th, attended by Song Ziwen, Shi Qingyang, Chen Shuren, Liu Ruiheng, Zhu Jiahua, Luo Wengan, and Chen Shaokuan. Chairman Song Ziwen resolved the following important cases:

(1) Li Zhigang, member of the Shaanxi Provincial Government and Director of Civil Affairs, resigned from his concurrent position as Director of Civil Affairs, and member Hu Yimin resigned from his position. Approved. Appoint Wang Quzhang as a member of the Shaanxi Provincial Government and Director of Civil Affairs.

(2) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs submitted a case in which Hong Zhong, Director of the Ordnance Department, resigned, and Yu Dasui was appointed to succeed him. Passed.

(3) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs submitted a case in which Wang E, Commander of the Jiangning Fortress Area, was relieved of his position, and Qian Lunti was appointed to succeed him. Passed.

(4) Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs submitted a case in which Liu Yi, Commander of the Independent 32nd Brigade, was dismissed, and Bai Tianmin was appointed to fill the position. Passed.

(5) Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry submitted a case in which Jiang Xiuqing, Director of the Marine Fisheries Administration of the Fujian-Guangdong Area, resigned, and Tan Boyi was appointed to succeed him. Passed.

(6) Minister Huang of the Ministry of Interior Affairs submitted a case for amending Articles 5, 10, and 14 of the Provincial Government Organization Law for the Second Interior Affairs Conference and changing the original four departments of the provincial government to three or four departments. The original amendment draft was attached and transferred for review. Passed. Sent to the Political Conference.

(7) Minister Luo of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs submitted a case for establishing a French Consulate Branch in Lyon, listing the estimated expenses and requesting review. Passed. (8) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Education, Minister Huang of the Ministry of Interior Affairs, and Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry jointly submitted a case based on the Central Agricultural Extension Committee's request to amend the Agricultural Extension Regulations, attaching the amendment draft and requesting review. Passed.

Regular Meeting of the Control Yuan 25

Nanjing: The Control Yuan held its 22nd meeting on the morning of the 24th, attended by Yu Youren, Ding Weifen, and Supervisory Commissioners Gao Youtang, etc., more than ten people. (1) It was decided to amend Article 3 of the Control Yuan's Review Rules. The review report on impeachment cases must be completed within one month at the latest. If there is a request for urgent relief measures attached, it must be completed within five days, but under special circumstances, the president may be requested to extend it. (2) Regarding the dismissal of appointed personnel such as disaster relief examinations, etc., when the impeachment case cannot be submitted, what method should be used for relief? It was decided to submit it to the Central Political Conference for a decision on the method. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

Control Yuan Establishes Regional Supervisory Envoys 26

Regulations Have Been Submitted to the Government for Record

Nanjing: In order to clarify official governance and alleviate the suffering of the people, the Control Yuan passed twelve articles of the Supervisory Envoy's Circuit Inspection Regulations on December 28 of last year, dividing the country into several supervisory districts, each with one supervisory envoy, serving a term of one year, patrolling and inspecting within their respective districts. For illegal and derelict behavior of public officials in the district, if it is deemed that the circumstances are serious and require rapid relief, in addition to filing an impeachment case, the responsible chief may be directly notified to take rapid relief measures. Ordinary cases are still subject to the procedures of Article 5 of the Impeachment Law. The regulations were submitted to the government for record on January 17. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 24th)

Nanjing: The Regulations on Circuit Inspection by Supervisory Envoys of the Control Yuan have been approved by the National Government for record. The full text consists of eleven articles, with the following contents: (1) The term of office of the supervisory envoy is set at one year. (2) The impeachment case filed by the supervisory envoy shall be in writing, but in case of emergency matters, it may be submitted by telegram first. (3) In order to exercise their powers, the supervisory envoys may inquire or investigate archives and registers from various official agencies and other public institutions within the supervisory district to which they are assigned. If there are any questions, the responsible personnel shall be responsible for providing detailed answers. (4) For illegal or derelict behavior of public officials in the supervisory district to which they are assigned, if it is deemed that the circumstances are serious and require rapid relief, in addition to filing an impeachment, the responsible chief may be directly notified to take rapid relief measures. If the responsible chief does not take rapid relief measures, they shall be held responsible when the impeached person is punished. (5) The supervisory envoy may accept reports from the people regarding illegal or derelict behavior of public officials, but shall not approve or answer them. (6) The supervisory envoy may establish an administrative office within the supervisory district to which they are assigned. (7) The supervisory envoy shall be governed by the provisions of the Law on the Protection of Supervisory Commissioners. (8) The supervisory envoy and their subordinates shall not take over local supplies, banquets, or gifts. (Special dispatch on the 23rd)

Proposal to Protect the Domestic Textile Industry 53

Nanjing, Chen Gongbo previously proposed a plan to protect the domestic textile industry at the Third Plenary Session, and the Central Political Council handed it over to the Ministry of Finance for review. The results are summarized as follows: 1. The Sino-Japanese reciprocity agreement, which expires in May of the 22nd year, should be completely revoked. 2. Increase import duties on cotton cloth, which should be at least doubled compared to the current tax rate. 3. Actively improve cotton production to reduce the need for textile mills to purchase foreign cotton. When cotton production has made considerable progress in both quality and quantity, further increase import duties on cotton and simultaneously increase duties on yarn and cloth. 4. For products from Chinese factories, the amount of tax collected, equivalent to the import duty on foreign yarn and cloth, should be used as a reward to suppress the development of foreign cotton production in China. (Special dispatch from the 24th)

Movement to Restore Silver Coinage in the US Congress 80

Washington, National News Agency, 23rd, a movement has now been launched in the US Congress with the aim of adopting the plan proposed by Briand 36 years ago, re-establishing silver as currency, and simultaneously reducing the price of gold dollars to promote economic progress. Senator Werner declared today that he will propose a plan to re-coin silver at a gold-silver ratio of sixteen to one in order to urge Congress to discuss the silver issue. His plan will be used as an amendment to the Glass Banking Reform Act so that it can be considered sooner, as the Glass Act is already under consideration in the committee and will be scheduled in the Senate earlier than any new bill. At the same time, Senator Borah advocated reducing the price of gold dollars, claiming today during the discussion of the balanced budget issue that the budget balance cannot be discussed until taxpayers themselves balance their income and expenditure. Today, because the government insists on maintaining the gold standard, the economy has been greatly affected. Not only has it lost foreign markets, but domestic markets have also been seized by low-cost goods from countries that have abandoned the gold standard, resulting in the decline of people's livelihoods. Furthermore, all economic problems between countries should also be resolved. There is the possibility of adjusting trade conditions, but it must be through the joint efforts of all countries.

German Political Situation Still Chaotic 81

Rumors of Cabinet Reshuffle Rampant

Berlin, National News Agency, 23rd, although the Nazi Party's parade held a few days ago did not cause any accidents, rumors of an imminent cabinet reshuffle are rampant again. It is said that the current Schleicher government will resign, and will be succeeded by a mixed cabinet of distinctly right-wing and extremist nature. After that, it will reverse the policies of the Schleicher cabinet, absolutely not cooperate or reach an understanding with the Catholic Center Party, and will disregard the interests of the masses behind the Center Party and the left wing. The reason for this political change is that Schleicher has expressed a stubborn and unyielding attitude, contrary to the expectations of the various right-wing parties. Therefore, the various right-wing parties are now working hard to connect separately and organize the situation of restoring parliamentary government.

Italy Follows Britain's Footsteps in Requesting Negotiations on War Debts; US Expresses Welcome 82

Washington, National News Agency, 23rd, Italy has followed in Britain's footsteps and requested the United States to open discussions on war debts after the new president takes office on March 4th. The request 　 has been delivered to the US State Department by the Italian Ambassador today. It is expected that the United States will grant Italy's request because Italy has also paid the installment due in December.

Rome, Havas, 24th, US Secretary of State Stimson will meet with Italian Ambassador to the United States Rosso, stating that if Italy sends a delegation to the United States to discuss war debt issues soon, he would be very welcoming.

US Constitutional Amendment Established 83

President and Members of Congress Take Office Earlier

Effective October of this Year

Jefferson, National News Agency, 23rd, the Norris constitutional amendment, which changes the inauguration dates of the President and members of Congress, has been approved by the Missouri State Legislature today, reaching the legal number and being established. The amendment stipulates that after each election, the new Congress will convene on January 3rd, and the new President will take office on January 20th. However, this amendment will not take effect until October of this year. Therefore, Roosevelt will still take office on March 4th as usual, but his four-year term will be shortened by more than 40 days, and his salary will be reduced by 10,954 yuan.

German representative Du 　ne declared opposition to the draft treaty on arms limitation, the reason being that Germany did not participate in the discussions when the treaty was drafted. It has now been decided to review the draft treaty again, and Germany has been asked to send representatives to cooperate in the discussions.

Ju Wu has now gathered troops and is heading to the Rehe border to work desperately. With a little assistance, they can continue their previous efforts. All assistance and donations will be given to General Zhu for forwarding, etc. It has been found that the area controlled by this department is strategically important, and the Japanese army attacked it fiercely for a reason. Although forced by circumstances, tens of thousands of people are hiding in various counties in Eastern Liaoning and can still inflict considerable punishment on the enemy at the necessary time. Recently, there have been fierce battles with the enemy in Qingyuan Nankouqian and Jinchuan Gannanjiaan. Tang Jun is also on the Rehe border, gathering the old troops totaling six to seven thousand people, planning to go to Eastern Liaoning at the appropriate time and restore the old territory. Their ambition is very strong. I hope that you will give them strong assistance so that they can achieve their goals. 　The Jilin-Heilongjiang People's Support Association is extremely grateful.

As for the organization of the fleet: (1) First Fleet - First Battle Squadron, Second Battle Squadron, Third Battle Squadron, First Torpedo Squadron, First Submarine Squadron, (2) Second Fleet - Fourth Battle Squadron, Fifth Battle Squadron, Second Torpedo Squadron, Second Submarine Squadron, First Aviation Squadron, (3) Third Fleet stationed in Shanghai, First Overseas Fleet stationed in Shanghai, Second Foreign Fleet stationed in North China, Training Fleet for ensign candidates distant 　sea use.

(Note) Honolulu and Singapore are exceptions.

It is reported that since 1927, the ports in the islands under Japanese mandate in the Pacific have increased threefold compared to the original. The United States believes that this port reconstruction violates the League of Nations' mandate treaty, as Japan is reconstructing the island bays into fortresses as bases for the army and navy in preparation for war. Therefore, at the meeting of the Mandate Committee last November, the committee members raised serious questions to the Japanese representative Ito Shushi. Recently, the diplomatic circles in Geneva have paid close attention to this issue, believing that Japan's solid defense of the South Pacific islands will endanger the transportation between Honolulu and the Philippines, and also worry that if Japan withdraws from the League of Nations, it will have strong facilities in the Pacific. It is rumored that the US government has telegraphed its ambassador to Rome to raise the issue to the chairman of the committee, Dadley. However, the US State Department denied the matter.

Enemy Attempts to Attack Rehe Fail 86

Forces Will Cross the Shi River to Capture Luanzhou

Then Attack Rehe from Lengkou and Xifengkou

Disturbances Around Tianjin and Beiping Intensify

Tianjin Correspondence: The silence on the Shi River and Shimen front lines has lasted for over ten days. Enemy aircraft bombings continue between Kailu and Fuxin, where tens of thousands of righteous soldiers are holding strategic positions with the support of Rehe troops, sufficient to cope with the situation. However, the enemy at Nanling Chaoyang Temple has attempted several attacks without success. The enemy planned to deploy six traitorous armies (two each under Yu Zhishan, Cheng Guorui, and Zhang HaiPeng) as the vanguard for attacking Rehe. Unexpectedly, many in the traitorous armies, deeply aware of righteousness, could not bear to kill their compatriots and deserted with their weapons, especially Cheng Guorui's troops, which are almost completely disbanded. This is because Cheng's troops are mostly composed of armed civilians from western Liaoning who were forced into service due to the oppressive environment and are not willing to betray their country. The enemy's unreliability of the traitorous armies has dealt a blow to their plans to attack Rehe. Recently, they have been digging trenches and building fortifications with electric fences in the Beipiao, Chaoyang Temple, and Nanling areas, indicating a shift to a defensive posture and the search for new, quicker routes to attack Rehe. According to a military expert, Japanese soldiers are extremely arrogant. Due to the Northeast Army's policy of non-resistance, they see the Northeast Army as mere deadwood. After occupying Shanhaiguan, they thought it would be like occupying Jinzhou, with the Northeast Army retreating and the matter being over. However, the soldiers and civilians of North China share a common hatred of the enemy, and international sentiment cannot be entirely exploited by the Japanese. The Japanese militarists seem unwilling to make too many enemies, so they only talk about taking Rehe as a problem of the puppet Manchurian state, temporarily setting aside Beiping and Tianjin, because Rehe has no American or European residents or businesses, which would not cause the intervention of the powers. As for their planned attack on Rehe, they have divided it into several routes. The three routes of attacking Kailu from Tongliao, Suidong from Zhangwu, and Fuxin from Xintun have already failed. The attack on Chaoyang from Nanling is also facing difficulties. Currently, only the route of attacking Lingyuan from Suizhong has not been tried. They are transporting munitions and food to Suizhong for a desperate attempt. If this route also proves difficult, they will inevitably cross the Shi River westward, attempting to seize the line of the river, and attack Chengde and Jianchang from Lengkou and Xifengkou. However, the Chinese army has already established defenses west of the Shi River, and it is doubtful whether the enemy will succeed. According to an observation by a certain important person, the enemy wants to seize the key areas of Rehe and will provoke incidents in Beiping and Tianjin to disrupt our rear defenses. Recently, Major General Umezu, Chief of Staff Koishihara, Colonel Doihara, and Advisor Sakahara have arrived in Tianjin and are the main figures planning disturbances in Beiping and Tianjin. It is said that the Tianjin plainclothes teams are still under the responsibility of Doihara. Since Hao Peng, the commander of the puppet North China People's Autonomous Salvation Army, was arrested in Beiping, a group of remaining cadres has held several secret meetings and, after reorganization by Doihara, have been reorganized into groups of ten, each group with a Japanese person as the leader, and every ten groups forming a team, with two Japanese people as the leader and deputy leader, directing everything. It is widely rumored that they plan to launch an incident in Tianjin on the anniversary of the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, with Beiping responding in support, but this news may not be reliable.

(January 22nd)

A Japanese Soldier's Diary 87

War Spoils of Our Army Near Xinlitun

A diary of a Japanese soldier, Watanabe Akihiko, was sent by a certain gentleman serving in the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army. It is said that on the 9th and 10th of this month, our army had fierce battles with the Japanese army near Xinlitun. The diary was found on the body of Watanabe Akihiko, who died in the battle against the Japanese Oham.

The cover is made of yellow cloth with black and red sawtooth lines printed on the front, followed by the word ( ). Below are printed the words "(Showa 7th Year Army Diary)" and "(Sakura Tadaharu Supervised)", etc. On the bottom is written in blue ink "(Murai Brigade, Cavalry 2nd Platoon, 4th Squad, Watanabe Akihiko)," the characters somewhat rough.

The diary starts from December 17th, Showa 7th year and ends on August 8th, Showa 8th year, totaling twenty-three days. Combined with what is written on the flyleaf, there are twenty-four entries. The diary is written in pencil and blue ink pen. The pencil writings are blurred and difficult to read. Here are selected the clearer and more significant entries, such as the text on the flyleaf and the entries from December 23rd and 26th of last year and January 5th of this year, translated as follows:

Looking at Watanabe's entire diary, his resentment of military service, his constant fear of death, and his unwillingness to fight against the Chinese are evident between the lines. He even criticizes his government's militaristic policies and deeply feels that life is tasteless, his situation pitiable, his emotions lamentable. If one Watanabe feels this way, many Japanese soldiers probably feel the same way. From this, we can gain two insights:

1. Over the years, the militarists in Japan have been tyrannical, the politics chaotic, the economy in panic, and the ideology radical. Those with insight have long known that crises lurk everywhere, and the path is dangerous. Yet, the Japanese army still does not reflect, but instead engages in militarism and intensifies its invasion of neighboring countries, hoping to divert its people's attention and maintain its own position. Little do they know that the army they rely on to invade neighboring countries has undergone a great change in thought and is no longer blindly obedient and willing to be exploited. If our people can vow to defend themselves to the death and thoroughly resist, then the awakening of the Japanese people can be expected soon.

2. The Japanese militarists, intoxicated by the victories of the Sino-Japanese War and the Russo-Japanese War, often boast to the world about the "imperial martial spirit" and the "power of the imperial army," as if the bravery and skill of the Japanese army are truly invincible. Now, after reading this diary and witnessing the Shanghai Incident, we know that the so-called "imperial martial spirit" and "power" are limited, and their fear and cowardice are even greater than others. Therefore, those with lofty ideals should deeply consider their responsibilities of resisting Japan and saving the nation, and only by fighting to the death can we achieve victory. Attached is an excerpt of the diary from January 21st.

Diary Excerpts:

Text on the Diary's Flyleaf: Our enemies are not the Chinese. The fields of Manchuria are not our battlefields. Our enemies are not so much the Chinese as they are the Japanese, the Japanese people should awaken from their self-respect, awaken from humanism. Now, the enemy country of China is gradually changing under our support, perhaps becoming a more powerful nation than us. Why should we fight against such an enemy?

December 27th: Tonight, I learned that the deployment is certain. The officers of the company are busy beyond words. Electric lights have been installed in the camp.

December 18th: Preparing to move out. There are many discussions, including with Watanabe-kun. The names of the soldiers going on expedition are announced, and my name is also on the list. Clothes, blankets, and other items are distributed.

December 19th: Assigned to the mobilized company. Mother, Hitoshi, and Shiro came to see me off at noon. My mother's strong mind, without shedding a tear, secretly pleases me. To comfort those left behind, I find it difficult to sit opposite them.

December 20th: Very busy with preparations. We inspect our military uniforms at one point. The division commander and brigade commander come to give instructions, roughly saying, "Soon they will become subjects under our rule, so if you kill someone, you should feel some sorrow. Pay attention to your health," etc. We also take a photo as a farewell memento. We bow and pay our respects to the military flag and the portrait of the Emperor. Uncle Uebayashi comes to see me off. I tell him not to worry about Mother. Several groups of people carrying lanterns come to the camp gate to send us off with cheers.

December 21st: Wake up at 1:30 AM. Depart from the camp at 3:30 AM. My horse is in good spirits and full of energy. Loading is completed at 5:30 AM. Head to the station. Depart at 8:00 AM. At Seto, the mother and friend of Fujiwara come to see me off. In Okayama, I meet my older brother Tadashi and Mr. Tachiki. Get off at Ujina at 3:30 PM.

Stayed for one night, the last night on home soil. I couldn't sleep. I only fell asleep a little after one o'clock.

December 22nd: At 6:30 AM, load the horses onto the "Goso Maru." I take one step at a time. It is a moment of departure from the Japanese land. Although I didn't shed tears, I still felt uneasy. The ship departs at 3:00 PM. The welcoming military vessels are sailing alongside our ship. I wanted to respond to their shouts of "Banzai," but I couldn't. While others were shouting "Banzai," I remained silent. But I regret that I don't have the determination to die.

December 23rd: Anchored at Shimonoseki. The most annoying thing is the merchants on the pier who are selling their goods at high prices to those of us who are about to part with our homeland. It even makes me feel that there is no need to die to protect the country of these people. At 4:30 PM, the shadow of our homeland gradually disappears from our eyes. The waves at night are very big, and I feel physically and mentally uncomfortable.

December 24th: After 10:00 AM, I see the Korean Peninsula. I receive cold-weather gear and put it on. I look like a fur-clad Russian. Some people even laugh. No one would have thought that we would be dressed like this. Wearing this clothing makes me sweat even without working. Once entering the Yellow Sea, the seawater turns yellow, which startles people. Life seems long, but it is actually very short. Within this short period, there are still those who await to bloom like a flower of humanity, and the great people of the future still do not know how they will achieve their greatness.

December 25th: Breaking through the waves of the Yellow Sea, the ship gradually becomes calm. We sail towards Dalian. The almost full moon hangs high in the blue sky, silently blessing our comrades' future. Standing on the deck without wearing a cold-weather vest, I feel very cold. The climate is so different. The time is one hour slower than in the homeland. From these facts, I cannot help but foresee that we have already left our homeland and are about to reach our destination.

December 26th (Arrive in Dalian): I get on the deck and watch the white birds gradually fly in from the middle of the island, entering Dalian Commercial Port. At 7:30 AM, the landing begins, but I stand by the outpost of Private Ono, feeling that life is tasteless. Later, I talk to the secretary Nakata and am given sake to drink, which gives me some meaning in life. I think that making friends is nothing more than this. I start playing in the streets at 1:30 PM, taking an automobile to see all of Dalian's famous sights in order to get a good look at them. It is good that no enemy figures have been seen yet.

December 27th: Gather at 9:00 AM. Go to the (Expense Section) with Fang. Leave home at 12:00 PM. From 5:00 PM, I stroll through the streets of Dalian and the piers with my comrades, as if I were touring my homeland in a dream.

December 28th (Arrive in Fengtian): Arriving in Fengtian at 7:30 AM. The temperature is 13.5 degrees above zero, and there is nothing unbearable. We gather the horses in the courtyard of the Fengtian Medical University. Seeing my beloved horse with icicles on its muzzle and frost on its body, spending the night in the open air in the northern suburbs, a strange feeling arises in my heart. Hearing talk of leaving to fight in May after opening the horse, it is also a touching matter.

December 29th: Yesterday (Xisheng Hao) was crippled in the left leg by my neighbor, Tenmura-kun. It is truly pitiful. He had worked hard to reach the age of twenty, but all his affairs were ruined. Now that he has lost a horse, how will a cavalryman advance?

December 30th: Gathered at 7:30 AM. The whole company only rose at 8:30 AM. Its situation is known. Ride in the train. The cold wind invades, constantly howling. Who can think of the icicles on the muzzle and the frost on the tail? The money I brought from my mother disappeared. Anyway, money will eventually be gone. It doesn't matter, let it be.

December 31st: I wake up at 4:00 AM when I am sleeping soundly. Prepare for departure at 6:00 AM. Head to Fengtian Station. Because the railway destroyed by the plainclothesmen last night is being repaired, we extended our departure to 1:00 PM and departed for Dahushan. Speaking of New Year's Eve, we don't even have dinner. The officers are all concerned about military affairs. Moving northwest, we start at 5:00 PM. The three trains are unable to move forward. At 12:00 PM, we finally arrive at Dahushan Station, occupying the station before the enemy. I go to the horse stable on duty, standing in the fields of Manchuria, spending New Year's Eve.

January 1st: While sleeping, I tremble and resist as if I am about to freeze to death, lying in the cabin, quietly waiting for the dawn. At 6:00 AM, I eat a half-cooked breakfast that seems to be slightly spoiled. At the foot of Dahushan, the companies form a line and sing the New Year's song together, standing before the enemy in a quiet gathering. It is not an anniversary event. There are two or three families living in the station, and also three or four prostitutes. It has already become a family. Also, I am already thinking about yesterday's battle.

January 2nd: At 10:00 AM, we occupy a large house inhabited by good Chinese civilians. We rest our bodies in the empty house. The local Chinese politely urge us to work, which really makes us feel ashamed. But we eat in our mouths and don't say anything.

January 3rd: At noon, I receive the order from the flag leader and know that there are bandits in Black Mountain. So I think and move quickly, rushing in the wilderness, following the scout Yano, doing reconnaissance. I see a train, earnestly carrying folk flags and white flags, gradually approaching me. I immediately go back to report, only to find that the visitor is an American inspector. The officers nervously hold their guns, rushing onto the car like the wind, while they are holding a banquet, and I return in disappointment.

January 4th: Arrive at the county town. I don't see the bandits, but I see four heads hanging high on the telephone poles outside the city. Perhaps they are the bandits' heads. It doesn't seem like bandits are attacking. I originally planned to go, but the situation is unclear, and the dogs are barking loudly. I find a large courtyard to spend the night and wait for dawn. Then I vigorously whip my horse, rushing down the road, returning without any gains. On the way, I use a machine gun to do a trial shooting.

January 5th: There are no enemies, but we are forced to do exercises against imaginary enemies. Who knows the sadness in this? If anyone knows, they will sigh that this kind of exercise is a meaningless act. In the morning, we gather on horseback and do a dismounted battle exercise near Gotabuko (transliteration).

January 6th: Wake up at 5:00 AM and move towards the Badokou Mine. Our squad pushes large luggage and moves forward slowly. It is seven miles away. Today, the north wind is very strong, and my hands and feet are cold. I can't help but miss my hometown. Arrive at 4:00 PM. There is a large power plant controlled by the British. The interior layout of the house is splendid, which is very surprising.

January 7th: Wake up at 5:30 AM and move towards Xinlitun. Everything is scarce, and there is nothing surprising. Arrive at 4:00 PM, and we move into the large house where Zhang Xueliang's army used to live. In this way, we occupy new territory without fighting. To whom should we boast about the spirit of the Yamato man?

January 8th: Today is the anniversary of the founding of the army. We hold a parade on horseback in the large square in front of the station. We eat Chinese food and drink Japanese sake for lunch.

Bloody Tragedy of the Hankou City Election 88

Hankou Correspondence: The Hankou Special City Party Department has been reorganized by central government officials for three years but has not yet been formally established. Recently, it was finally decided to elect members of the Executive and Supervisory Committees to establish the Party Department. The election date was originally scheduled for the 20th of this month. However, the central election supervisors, Zeng Kuoqing and Fang Juezhen, were traveling from Nanjing on the Xinxing Lun when it ran aground in Jiujiang. The election was temporarily changed to the 21st. There are over 4,500 party members in Hankou City. They were designated to vote in ten districts. The venues had been arranged in advance, and military and police personnel were requested to maintain order. Zeng and Fang arrived in Hankou on the 20th and held an emergency meeting at the City Party Department. They instructed the reorganization committee members of the City Party Department on two matters: (1) all party membership cards are invalid. Only those who have a certificate from the City Party Department are allowed to enter the venue. (2) Party membership cards without a stamp or with insufficient stamps must be stamped to be valid for entry. On the 21st, at 9:00 AM, as snow fell, party members from each district voted at the designated locations. In addition to personally inspecting the venues, Zeng and Fang also sent Cai Shuzhong, Rao Zhenchang, Zhou Xiaoxi, Fang Chengyan, Zhou Jietian, Tong Hua, Zuo Zhenxin, Chen Minjian, Chen Zhiguang, and Du Shusi to supervise the elections in each venue. Because there were many candidates, there were many instances of coercion of voters and forced proxy voting on the spot, which led to disputes. Except for Districts 1, 3, 4, 5, 9, and 10, violent incidents occurred in Districts 2, 6, 7, and 8. Most party members in District 2 voluntarily withdrew from the meeting. In District 7, three people were injured in beatings. In District 8, one person was injured in beatings. Because the order was disrupted, the election was stopped and the ballot boxes were broken. Zeng and Fang immediately decided to stop the election altogether. They sent the injured party members Liu Fangying, Ding Xianben, Xia Dengxun, and Tang Xigen to the hospital for treatment. They also telegraphed the situation to the central government for instructions. It is rumored that this election will be completely invalid and will be rescheduled after the central government sends Liu to take charge. (January 21st)

Guangdong Province Strengthens National Defense 89

Ordering Large Quantities of Military Equipment from Foreign Merchants

Especially Active in Anti-Aircraft Defense Arrangements

The Shanghai-based English newspaper, the "North China Daily News," reported on the 16th, via their Hong Kong correspondent, that foreign merchants engaged in the arms trade are not experiencing an economic downturn. The military authorities in Guangzhou recently ordered several field guns, some of which were delivered today. Since the Japanese occupied Manchuria, the Guangzhou military authorities have been ordering large quantities of rifles, mortars, and machine guns from Hong Kong foreign merchants to prevent a second Shanghai Incident by the Japanese. Recently, the authorities have also realized the importance of field guns and artillery in national defense and have ordered several more. It is reported that they will be installed at the Yantang Army University for officer training. The university's principal, General Chen Jitang, concurrently holds the position, so there are sufficient funds to make the school one of the key fortresses in the Southwest. Therefore, Hong Kong merchants who have dealings with European arms factories, especially Czech arms factories, are enjoying booming business. A British merchant in Hong Kong has secured an order for six anti-aircraft guns, but the buyer is surprisingly the Guangzhou Municipal Government. Mayor Liu Jiwen fears that Japanese aircraft will disrupt Guangzhou, so he purchased these to defend Guangzhou City. Half of the funds came from public donations, and the other half was allocated from the city's coffers. Japan has only one 900-ton gunboat stationed in Shamian in Guangzhou and has no naval or army troops stationed there. It seems that there is no fear of a Japanese military invasion. However, the Cantonese people are on guard against a surprise aerial bombardment of Guangzhou by the Japanese, so they are preparing in advance. Aircraft carriers have also been coveted by naval officers in Guangzhou. Recently, a group of officers came to Hong Kong to visit the British aircraft carrier Hermes, which sailed to the sea to conduct flight exercises for them. General Weng Zhaoyuan, who valiantly defended Shanghai's Baoshan County during the January 28th Incident last year, has returned to Hong Kong after visiting the Philippines. General Weng studied aviation in France and has superb flying skills. This time, he raised a large amount of air defense funds from overseas Chinese in the Philippines, which will be used to establish an air force team for the 19th Route Army. The Hong Kong overseas Chinese specially held a grand banquet to welcome him. Weng gave a speech on the situation of the Japanese army bombing Wusong at that time, which made the listeners resentful.

Guangdong Province Establishes Industrial Bureau in Hainan 90

Presiding Over the Development of Industries in Hainan Island

Guangzhou Correspondence: The communist bandits in Hainan Island have been gradually suppressed. The island's forests and marine products are abundant and urgently need to be developed to create profits. The Department of Construction recently petitioned the provincial government to establish a Hainan Island Industrial Bureau to manage the affairs. The provincial government has approved the establishment and appointed Zhu Chini as the director of the bureau. Zhu has already taken office and traveled with the staff to handle the matter. It is said that the Industrial Bureau is directly under the provincial Department of Construction. The internal organization includes technicians, engineers, and assistant technicians, each in a certain number, to be responsible for various technical affairs. Depending on the complexity of the affairs, additional staff may be added, and local experienced industrial experts may be hired as design consultants. If necessary for the development of industries, agricultural and forestry reclamation farms, animal husbandry farms, various industrial manufacturing plants, and various exhibition halls may be established. The matters to be handled by the bureau are defined as follows: (1) matters related to industrial administration, (2) matters related to the development of fishery and salt mines, (3) matters related to the improvement and promotion of agriculture, industry, commerce, and related matters, (4) matters related to the investigation, design, management, and planning of all industries, (5) matters related to assisting the development of domestic products and improving industries. As for the industries that should be developed first: (1) increase food production and improve seeds, (2) increase livestock production and improve quality, (3) improve fishing and manufacturing, (4) trial planting and improvement of cotton and hemp, (5) extensive planting and improvement of local specialties such as rubber, coconuts, betel nuts, jackfruit, and coffee, (6) manufacturing of various agricultural and industrial products, (7) salt manufacturing. The director of the bureau is responsible for all the above-mentioned management and operation matters. The director has two departments under him, each with two section chiefs and several staff members, who carry out their duties under the director's orders. (January 18th)

Air Defense Equipment in Fujian Province 91

Weng Zhaoyuan Arrives in Fujian to Discuss Organizing Volunteer Army

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Pacification Commissioner's Office in Fujian Province previously recruited over one hundred retired air force officers and generals from Guangdong to come to Fujian to establish an aviation squadron in the province. However, Fujian only has seven small aircraft, which are mainly used to transport important people and are difficult to use in actual warfare. A month ago, Weng Zhaoyuan and Zou Minchu were specially sent to British and American colonies in Southeast Asia to promote aviation to save the nation and raise funds to purchase fighter planes. Now Weng has completed his mission and returned to the country. He arrived in the province from Shanghai the other day and reported to Jiang Guangnai and Cai Tingkai about the promotion situation in the American colonies. He said that the trip was very successful and received great sympathy from overseas Chinese. In various ports of the Philippines, twenty-six aviation associations were organized, with over 12,000 members, raising over 700,000 Philippine pesos, which can be used to purchase fifteen fighter planes. The funds are temporarily deposited in local banks by the associations. He is currently negotiating with Cai Tingkai to organize a volunteer army to go north to resist the Japanese. It is reported that Weng asked Cai to select two elite brigades from the 19th Route Army, and Weng will also gather the old troops of the volunteer army he trained in Suzhou and Wuxi last year, forming another brigade, obtaining a total of 15,000 men to lead to the border to fight the enemy. The detailed plan is under discussion. As for the province's anti-aircraft defense plan, according to an aviation team officer, the important commercial ports of Fujian Province, such as Fuzhou, Xiamen, Quanzhou, Xinghua, and Sandu, are all located along the coast, close to Taiwan, and are subject to the threat of enemy aircraft at any time. It is estimated that the value of buildings in each port averages no less than 50 to 60 million yuan, which is the essence of the province. If they are bombed by enemy aircraft, they will be instantly turned to dust. Therefore, building air defenses is the most urgent task for Fujian Province at present. As for the steps, the first is to purchase more anti-aircraft guns to prevent enemy aircraft from approaching, and the second is to equip fighter planes so that they can counter the enemy. However, the most urgent task is still to place more anti-aircraft guns. Roughly speaking, five ports need around 250 anti-aircraft guns to be useful. The 250 anti-aircraft guns are worth about 7 million yuan. The government may have difficulty raising this large amount of money at once, so it hopes that the people will raise the money themselves in the short term, while the government focuses on purchasing fighter planes. With division of labor and cooperation, it will be easy. (January 19th)

New Facilities in Guangxi 92

Relief for Rural Areas and Military Reclamation

Nanning Correspondence: The Guangxi province has made significant progress in developing roads, rigorously training the militia, and strictly enforcing bans on gambling and opium. These efforts have already been realized. Recently, they have also launched relief programs for rural areas and military reclamation projects. The general situation is as follows: (1) Rural Relief: Guangxi's rural areas have been less affected by external influences and have not yet fallen into bankruptcy. However, the local government is concerned that various construction projects may increase the burden on the people. In addition to reducing the number of standing soldiers to alleviate the financial burden and relieve the people, the government has decided to allocate a certain percentage of income from military and political circles each month, starting this year, to be specifically deposited as funds for lending to farmers and providing relief to rural villages. This income donation method only involves a portion of the military budget, and it is estimated that approximately 100,000 yuan can be obtained each month, and over 1 million yuan each year. The distribution procedures will be managed by the Guangxi Provincial Bank's branch offices. (2) Preparing for Military Reclamation: Guangxi has a relatively sparse population and a large amount of wasteland. In order to increase production and reduce the burden of military expenses, the local government has decided to adopt a system of military land reclamation, starting this year. They are currently drafting implementation rules and regulations and are initially selecting land in Guilin, Liuzhou, and Longzhou to build houses and purchase seeds and farming tools, with the aim of starting operations in the shortest possible time. This matter is of great importance to the future of agriculture, so all sectors are eagerly anticipating its success. (January 17th)

Wuxi

Seven Robberies in Two Days 93

In the past two days, seven robbery cases have occurred. A summary is as follows: (1) On the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, the 25th eastbound train, at approximately 7 p.m. on the evening of the 23rd, while passing Gaozi Station, a thief suddenly jumped out from among the second-class passengers. He drew a sharp knife, intimidated the passengers, stripped a passenger with luxurious clothing of his fur coat, and robbed him of over 100 yuan in cash. He then jumped off the train and fled. After the incident, military police from Zhenjiang Station pursued him on a motorcycle, but were unable to apprehend him. (2) Shi Jiusheng, a resident of Sitou Town in the 5th district, who was a man of some wealth, was robbed of over 200 yuan in cash, as well as clothing and jewelry worth over 1,000 yuan, by bandits late in the evening of the previous day. Shi's elderly mother was also injured. (3) More than ten dan of rice were stolen from the Shanggu Temple in Nanfangquan, in the 14th district, on the previous night. (4) Jin Bu, who ran a goose farm outside the South Gate in Laoyaotoupu, was robbed of forty-seven geese by bandits at approximately 3 a.m. yesterday morning. (5) Chen Wenming, a resident of Zhoujing, Longzhuxiang, in the southern countryside, had thirteen dan of white rice stolen by bandits last night. (6) Lu Gun, a resident of Qiganxia, in the southern countryside, had eight or nine dan of white rice, as well as clothing, etc., worth over 100 yuan, stolen by thieves last night. (7) Chen Jinbao, a resident of Lengshuxiang, Jiangbo Bridge, in the 2nd district, was also robbed yesterday morning, suffering losses of over 100 yuan.

Changzhou

Four Hundred New Rickshaws Added 94

The rickshaws managed by the Wuyi Police Bureau originally numbered 600. Over the years, there have been requests to add more, but they have not been implemented. Recently, there was another request to add more. On the 23rd, the county government held a county administration meeting to discuss the matter and decided to add 400 rickshaws. It will be implemented as soon as approval is obtained from the Construction Department.

Yangzhou

Students from Huaibao Robbed by Bandits 95

Yesterday (the 23rd), about twenty male and female students from the Huaibao area, who were returning home from various schools in Yangzhou for the holidays, encountered several bandits carrying guns on the road to Luzhen, because the weather was snowy, the river was frozen, and boats could not travel. The bandits seized the students, their luggage, and books, and fired shots to intimidate them.

Ningbo

Young Man Commits Suicide Out of Worry for the Country 96

Zhu Baochu, from Fangjia Village in Cixi Shushan, who was just over twenty years old, used to study at Chengzhong Middle School in Shanghai. The outbreak of the Shanghai War last year deeply affected him. He immediately reported home and spent his days worrying about national affairs, shutting himself away. Upon reading the recent news of the loss of Rehe, he cried out in agony. Then, the other day, Zhu Baochu was in his room, beating his chest and stomping his feet, singing mournful songs and drinking alone, until midnight, when he committed suicide by taking poison. It is said that the deceased left behind several suicide notes.

Notes on Robbery Cases 97

(1) Yesterday morning (the 23rd) at approximately 2 a.m., four robbers came to the house of Hu Fusheng, the owner of the Kaifu Ji Soy Sauce Factory in Yindong Yu'ai, broke down the door, and ransacked the house at will for an hour. It is estimated that they stole silver, jewelry, etc., worth over 4,000 yuan. (2) Zhou Zufa, a resident of Xiangshahetou in Shishi, Zhenhai 1st District, who makes a living by rowing boats, was suddenly attacked by fifteen bandits at midnight last night. Seven thieves stood guard outside, while six thieves entered the house to rob it. All the valuables in the house were stolen, and Zhou Zufa's left foot was cut with a knife.

Shangyu

Chunze Company Robbed 98

At approximately 7 p.m. on the 20th, two bandits suddenly broke into the Chunze Reclamation Company in Xiaojie, east of Yucheng, and stole all the cash reserves in the safe, amounting to several thousand yuan. Another bandit used scissors to injure the head of Ah Zhao, a worker from Gongzhai Street, who was in the company, and looted him of 60 yuan. At that time, the merchant militia stationed in the Chamber of Commerce had already heard the alarm and rushed to the He Bridge, dozens of steps away from the company, and fired shots to intimidate the bandits. The two bandits then successively fled and escaped. Two bandits were captured. Afterwards, the company checked the losses and found some of the stolen cash left behind by the bandits in the store, leaving a shortage of 1,380 yuan. The weapons and grenades belonging to the bandits were made of mud and coated with paste. They were abandoned on the ground as they fled. As for the captured bandit, he confessed that his name was Wang Chuanfa, and his accomplice who escaped was named Wang Asan. The two men confessed that the robbery was initiated by Wang Asan. Since the incident, all businesses have been wary and closed early.

Xiaoshan

Maid Abuse Case Sentences to Four Years of Imprisonment 99

Shen Shu, a butcher from Fengyan Bridge Lower Street in Dongmen, Xiaoshan, was accused of abusing his maid, Xiang, to death, and abandoning her body in an open space behind the Zhulin Temple. The county court investigated the truth of the case and the town chief, Lu Puyue, confirmed the facts. The county court detained Mr. and Mrs. Shen for questioning, and summoned the original matchmaker, Grandma Qi Baosheng, to confront them. The truth of the case was then revealed. Yesterday, Prosecutor Zheng came to court and sentenced Mr. and Mrs. Shen to four years in prison each, and Grandma Qi Baosheng to one year.

Hefei

Large Fire at Zhang Jingda's Residence 100

The former residence of Zhang Jingda, a high-ranking official of the Qing Dynasty, located opposite Longmen Lane on West Street in the city, was vast in scale and had numerous buildings. It is currently occupied by the rear service office of the Third Army, with the rear building being the residence of Li Weichuan from Fengtai County. At 10 a.m. on the 12th, a fire broke out in Li's residence due to carelessness while warming himself by the fire. The fire spread to the front building. The gasoline stored by the Third Army ignited, causing the fire to spread rapidly. The rear service office immediately moved the military supplies and reported the incident by telephone to various agencies. County Magistrate Wang, the Public Security Bureau Chief, and the Chief of the Inspection Office, Dong, immediately ordered a large number of soldiers and police to supervise the fire hoses to put out the fire. It was not until 1 p.m. that the fire was extinguished. Three five- or six-story buildings were burned down, resulting in losses of approximately tens of thousands of yuan. When the fire was at its height, the post office next door was affected. At that time, because of the urgency of the situation, there was chaos. Work was suspended for half a day on the afternoon of the 12th.
